Inheritance of a Fetus: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the share of an existing heir when a fetus is present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on the share of an existing child when a fetus is present, identify the mufta bihi opinion, and apply the conditions for the fetus to inherit.

Core Idea
The fetus inherits if born alive; its share is suspended, and the existing child's share depends on the assumed maximum offspring.

When a man dies leaving both an existing child and a pregnant wife, the inheritance of the existing child is uncertain because the fetus may be one or more children. The Hanafi imams disagreed on how many children a woman can carry at once, leading to different shares for the existing child. This lesson unpacks that dispute and the conditions for the fetus to inherit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic scenario and rule
When a man dies leaving only a pregnant wife (no existing children), all wealth is suspended until birth. When there is an existing child, the dispute arises.
The suspension is to preserve the rights of the potential heir(s).
2
Understand each imam's assumption
Abu Hanifa assumed a maximum of four children in one womb, Abu Yusuf assumed one (the usual), and Muhammad assumed two. These assumptions determine the share given to the existing child.
The shares are fractions: for a son: 1/5 (Abu Hanifa), 1/2 (Abu Yusuf), 1/3 (Muhammad). For a daughter: 1/9, 1/2, 1/3 respectively.
3
Trace the reasoning (qiyas)
Each imam reasoned from observed maximums. The existing child receives a share corresponding to the possible number of fetuses. The less the assumed maximum, the larger the share for the existing child.
Abu Yusuf's view became the fatwa because it is the most common scenario.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's saying: the existing child (son or daughter) gets half of the estate, the rest suspended for the fetus.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah also adopts this as the relied-upon view.
5
Apply the conditions for fetal inheritance
The fetus inherits only if born alive within six months of death (if marriage ongoing) or within two years of separation (if in 'idda). These are Hanafi maximum gestation periods.
If born later, the fetus is not considered an heir from the deceased.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن مات، وتَرَكَ حَمْلاً : وُقِفَ ماله حتى تضع امرأته في قول أبي حنيفة. وهذا إذا لم يكن للميت ولد سوى الحمل، أما إذا كان له ولد سواه : فإن كان ذكراً : أعطي خمس المال وأوقف أربعة أخماسه، وإن كان أنثى : أعطيت تُسع المال، وأوقف ثمانية أتساعه، وهذا قول أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف : يُعطى الابن نصف المال. وقال محمد : ثلث المال ؛ لأن المرأة لا تلد في العادة في بطن واحد أكثر من اثنين، فيستحق هذا الموجود الثلث. ولأبي يوسف : أنها تلد في العادة ولداً واحداً، فيجوز أن يكون ابناً. ولأبي حنيفة: أن أكثر ما تلد المرأة في بطن واحد أربعة، فيجوز أن يكون الحمل أربعة بنين، فيستحق الابن الخمس، والبنت تستحق التسع. والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف. هذا كله إذا عُرف وجوده في البطن، بأن جاءت به لأقل من ستة أشهر منذ مات المورث، أما إذا جاءت به لأكثر من ذلك: فلا ميراث له إذا كان النكاح قائماً. فإن كانت معتدة: إن جاءت به لأقل من سنتين منذ وقعت الفرقة : بموت أو طلاق فهو من جملة الورثة. كذا في «المستصفى».
And whoever dies leaving a fetus: his wealth is suspended until his wife gives birth, according to Abu Hanifa. This is if the deceased has no child other than the fetus. But if he has another child besides it: if it is a male: he is given one-fifth of the wealth and four-fifths are suspended; if it is a female: she is given one-ninth of the wealth and eight-ninths are suspended. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: the son is given half of the wealth. Muhammad said: one-third of the wealth; because a woman usually does not give birth to more than two in one womb, so this existing one deserves one-third. According to Abu Yusuf: she usually gives birth to one child, so it is possible that it is a son. According to Abu Hanifa: the most a woman gives birth to in one womb is four, so the fetus could be four sons, so the son deserves one-fifth, and the daughter deserves one-ninth. And the fatwa is according to the saying of Abu Yusuf. All this is if its existence in the womb is known, by her bringing it forth less than six months since the death of the testator. But if she brings it forth after that, then there is no inheritance for it if the marriage is ongoing. If she is in 'idda: if she brings it forth less than two years since the separation occurred, by death or divorce, then it is among the heirs. Thus in al-Mustasfa.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the inheritance of a fetus (haml). The basic ruling: when a man dies leaving a pregnant wife, his estate is suspended until she gives birth, because the fetus is a potential heir. The dispute arises when the deceased already has another child besides the fetus. Abu Hanifa considers the maximum possible number of children in one womb to be four, so he gives the existing child a conservative share: one-fifth if a son (assuming four sons could be born), one-ninth if a daughter (assuming four daughters? Actually the text says for a daughter one-ninth, which implies possibility of multiple daughters? Let me explain: if there is a son, Abu Hanifa gives him one-fifth, and suspends four-fifths for the potential four sons; similarly, if there is a daughter, he gives her one-ninth, suspending eight-ninths for the potential of four daughters? But the shares are based on the assumption that the fetus could be multiple children. Abu Yusuf assumes the usual maximum is one child, so gives half to the existing son (assuming the fetus could be one son), and suspends half. Imam Muhammad assumes up to two children, so gives one-third. The fatwa is according to Abu Yusuf. The passage also discusses conditions: the fetus inherits only if born within six months of death (if the marriage was valid) or within two years of separation (if the woman is in 'idda), which is the maximum period of gestation according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حمل (haml): A fetus in the womb that is a potential heir.
مستصفى (al-Mustasfa): A reference work by Imam al-Ghazali (in usul al-fiqh) or possibly a Hanafi work. Here it is cited as a source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa (mufta bihi), what share does an existing daughter receive when the deceased also leaves a pregnant wife?
A) One-ninth
B) One-half
C) One-third
D) One-fifth

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi on fetal inheritance: the existing child receives half the estate, the rest is suspended for the fetus, which inherits if born alive within the specified gestation periods.

Grandfather's Inheritance with Siblings: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on grandfather and siblings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on grandfather's inheritance with siblings and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between them.

Core Idea
Grandfather vs siblings: Abu Hanifa gives all to grandfather; Sahibayn make him share.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the grandfather (jadd) holds a unique position. While he is generally an 'asaba heir, his relationship with siblings is contested within the school itself. This short passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah presents the views of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), offering a clear example of intra-madhhab ikhtilaf that affects real inheritance distributions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa holds regarding grandfather and siblings. He says grandfather is more entitled (awla) and excludes siblings entirely, taking the whole inheritance as 'asaba.
This is analogous to a father who excludes brothers.
2
Identify the opposing view within the school
Note the Sahibayn's position: the grandfather does not exclude siblings but shares with them.
However, there is a safeguard: if sharing would reduce the grandfather's share below one-third, he is given one-third and siblings take the rest.
3
Analyze the reasoning (dalil) behind each view
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas jali: grandfather is an ancestor like father, so he excludes siblings by analogy. The Sahibayn rely on ijtihad: siblings also have a close relation, so the grandfather should not exclude them entirely; fairness dictates sharing, but with a minimum share for the grandfather.
No explicit proof is given in this passage; these are common explanations.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, if a grandfather and a sibling are the only heirs, the grandfather takes all. Under the Sahibayn, they share: if the estate is 120, grandfather gets his share of the 'asaba portion (e.g., with one full brother, they split 50/50 unless that gives grandfather less than 40, then he gets 40 and brother gets 80).
This difference has real financial implications for heirs.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Later Hanafi practice (as in most standard fatwa) adopts the Sahibayn's view, but this text does not specify. The student should be aware that the reliance varies.
In many Hanafi inheritance manuals, the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والجد أولى بالميراث من الإخوة عند أبي حنيفة، وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : يقاسمهم، إلا أن تنقصه المقاسمة من الثلث).
His saying: (And the grandfather is more entitled to the inheritance than the siblings according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: he shares with them, unless the sharing reduces him from one-third).
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This is a short passage presenting an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the inheritance of the grandfather when siblings exist. Abu Hanifa holds that the grandfather excludes siblings (i.e., takes the entire inheritance as 'asaba), similar to how a father excludes brothers. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the grandfather does not exclude siblings but shares with them, unless the siblings' shares would reduce the grandfather's portion to less than one-third; in that case, the grandfather is given one-third and the siblings take the remainder. This ruling is the subject of further elaboration elsewhere in Hanafi works. The passage does not specify the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
جد (jadd): The paternal grandfather (father's father).
إخوة (ikhwah): Siblings (full or consanguine brothers/sisters) in the context of inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, what happens to the grandfather's share if sharing with siblings would give him less than one-third?
A) Grandfather takes nothing
B) Grandfather takes one-third and siblings take the rest
C) Grandfather and siblings share equally
D) Grandfather takes the entire estate

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa excludes siblings in favor of the grandfather; the Sahibayn require sharing with a one-third minimum for the grandfather.

Grandfather's Inheritance with Brothers: Sahibayn's Method and Calculation
Intra-Hanafi dispute and calculation rules for grandfather with brothers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Sahibayn's method to calculate the grandfather's share in the presence of brothers, choosing among muqasama, thulth al-kull/thulth al-baqi, and sudus al-kull, and identify the best outcome.

Core Idea
The grandfather chooses the most beneficial of three options: equal division, one-third, or one-sixth.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the grandfather's position relative to brothers is disputed within the school. While Abu Hanifa held that the grandfather excludes brothers, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) introduced a protective rule: the grandfather shares with brothers but never falls below one-third. This lesson unpacks the Sahibayn's method for calculating the grandfather's share in various scenarios, with and without fixed-share heirs, using the examples from the matn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the presence of a fixed-share heir
Check if there is a sahib fard (e.g., daughter, wife). If yes, the grandfather has three options; if no, two options.
Fixed-share heirs are those with prescribed Quranic shares.
2
Compute options without a fixed-share heir
Calculate muqasama (equal division of entire estate among grandfather and brothers per capita) and thulth al-kull (1/3 of total estate). Compare to find the larger share for the grandfather.
Example: grandfather + 2 brothers: muqasama = 1/3 each, thulth al-kull = 1/3, equal.
3
Compute options with a fixed-share heir
First give the fixed share to the sahib fard. Then calculate: (1) muqasama of the residue (divide residue equally among grandfather and brothers), (2) thulth al-baqi (1/3 of residue), (3) sudus al-kull (1/6 of original total). Select the maximum for the grandfather.
The comparisons use the residue after the fixed share is paid.
4
Apply the comparison to the text examples
Work through each example: grandfather+1brother, +2brothers, +3brothers, with and without a daughter. Determine the best option in each case and note the resulting shares.
Pay attention to how the number of brothers affects the comparison.
5
Finalize the distribution
Assign the chosen share to the grandfather. The fixed-share heir takes his/her share. The remaining residue goes to the brothers equally (if any residue remains).
Brothers share equally as residuary heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والجد أولى بالميراث من الإخوة عند أبي حنيفة، وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : يقاسمهم، إلا أن تنقصه المقاسمة من الثلث). ثم على قولهما : للجد حالتان إحداهما : إذا لم يكن هناك صاحب فرض : فهو مخير بين المقاسمة وبين ثلث جميع المال. والثانية : إذا كان هناك صاحب فرض: فهو مخير بين ثلاثة أشياء: إما المقاسمة، أو ثلث ما بقي، أو سدس جميع المال. بيانه : جد وأخ: للجد: النصف، وللأخ: النصف. جد وأخوان: الثلث والمقاسمة هنا سواء. - جد وثلاثة إخوة : الثلث هنا خير له من المقاسمة. فإن كان معهم صاحب فرض: أعطي فرضه، ثم يُنظر إلى ثلث ما بقي، وإلى سدس جميع المال وإلى المقاسمة: يُنظر أولاً إلى ثلث ما بقي، وإلى سدس جميع المال : أيهما خير له، ثم يُنظر إلى خيرهما، وإلى المقاسمة : فأيهما كان خيراً له : كان له. بيانه: بنت وجد وأخٌ للبنت النصفُ، والباقي بينهما نصفان؛ لأن المقاسمة خير له من ثلث ما بقي، ومن سدس المال. جميع فإن كانا أخوين والمسألة بحالها فهنا ثلث ما بقي، وسدس جميع المال، والمقاسمة سواء. فإن كانوا ثلاثةً وهي بحالها فثلث الباقي، وهو سدس جميع المال خير له من المقاسمة.
His saying: (The grandfather has precedence in inheritance over the brothers according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He divides with them, unless the division reduces him from one-third). Then according to them: The grandfather has two states: One: When there is no fixed-share heir: he has the choice between division and one-third of the entire wealth. The second: When there is a fixed-share heir: he has the choice between three things: either division, or one-third of what remains, or one-sixth of the entire wealth. Its explanation: Grandfather and brother: for the grandfather half, for the brother half. Grandfather and two brothers: one-third and division here are equal. Grandfather and three brothers: one-third here is better for him than division. If there is a fixed-share heir with them: he [the fixed-share heir] is given his share, then consideration is given to one-third of what remains, and one-sixth of the entire wealth, and division: first look at one-third of what remains and one-sixth of the entire wealth: whichever is better for him, then look at the better of those two and at division: whichever is better for him, he gets it. Its explanation: Daughter, grandfather, and brother: the daughter gets half, and the rest between them in halves, because division is better for him than one-third of what remains and than one-sixth of the wealth. If they are two brothers and the case as it is, then here one-third of what remains and one-sixth of the entire wealth and division are equal. If they are three and the case as it is, then one-third of what remains, which is one-sixth of the entire wealth, is better for him than division.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage deals with the inheritance of the grandfather in the presence of brothers, highlighting an intra-Hanafi dispute. According to Abu Hanifa, the grandfather excludes the brothers entirely (he is closer). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the grandfather shares with the brothers, but with a protective rule: if division would give him less than one-third of the estate, he is entitled to one-third instead. The commentary then explains the mechanics on the Sahibayn's view. For cases without a fixed-share heir (e.g., no spouse or ascendant), the grandfather can choose between dividing the estate equally with the brothers (muqasama) or taking one-third of the entire estate. For cases with a fixed-share heir, the grandfather has three options: muqasama (division of the residue), one-third of the remainder after the fixed share, or one-sixth of the entire estate. He takes whichever is most beneficial. Several examples illustrate: with one brother, muqasama gives half which is better than one-third. With two brothers, muqasama gives one-third, same as the one-third option. With three brothers, one-third (of the total or remainder) is better than muqasama which would give one-fourth. The examples with a daughter (fixed-share heir getting half) show how to choose: for one brother, muqasama gives the grandfather half of the residue (1/4 of whole) which is better than one-third of residue (1/6) or one-sixth of whole (1/6). With two brothers, all options equal (1/6). With three brothers, one-third of residue (1/6) is best.

Key Terms
مقاسمة (muqasamah): Equal division of the inheritance or residue between the grandfather and the brothers.
صاحب فرض (sahib fard): An heir who receives a fixed Quranic share (e.g., daughter, spouse).
خير له (khayr lahu): More beneficial for him; the choice the grandfather makes to maximize his share.
ثلث ما بقي (thulth al-baqi): One-third of the residue after the fixed-share heir's portion.
سدس جميع المال (sudus al-kull): One-sixth of the entire estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, when there is a fixed-share heir, which of the following is NOT among the grandfather's options?
A) Muqasamah
B) Thulth al-baqi
C) Sudus al-kull
D) Rub' al-kull

Key Takeaway
Under the Sahibayn's view, the grandfather's share with brothers is the maximum of muqasama, one-third (of total or residue), and one-sixth, ensuring he never receives less than one-third.

The Grandfather's Two States with Siblings (Sahibayn's View)
Explains the two states of the grandfather with siblings according to the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Sahibayn's two-state rule for the grandfather with siblings and calculate his optimal share in various scenarios.

Core Idea
The grandfather receives the best of multiple shares — he chooses between muqasamah, one-third, or one-sixth.

This passage from Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira explains the independent view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on how the grandfather inherits alongside siblings. Unlike a fixed Quranic sharer, the grandfather's share is flexible: he gets the highest of several possible portions, depending on whether a fixed-share heir exists. Through worked examples, you will learn to identify the two states and apply the selection method.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two states
Without a fixed-share heir, the grandfather chooses between muqasamah (dividing equally with siblings) and one-third of the total estate. With a fixed-share heir, he has three options: muqasamah, one-third of the residue, or one-sixth of the total estate.
The grandfather is treated as a brother in muqasamah.
2
Apply the choice without a fixed-share heir
Compare muqasamah vs. one-third of total. Example: grandfather + 1 brother → muqasamah gives half, better than 1/3. Grandfather + 3 brothers → muqasamah gives 1/4, worse than 1/3 total, so choose 1/3.
The threshold is when siblings outnumber the grandfather by 2 or more.
3
Apply the choice with a fixed-share heir
First give fixed-share heir(s) their due. Then compare muqasamah of residue, one-third of residue, and one-sixth of total. Choose the best. Example: daughter (1/2), grandfather, brother → residue 1/2; muqasamah gives 1/4 each, which is better than 1/6 or 1/6.
Always compare the three after fixed shares.
4
Note the limiting principle from Zayd's madhhab
The grandfather's share never falls below one-sixth of the total estate. In combinations like two daughters, mother, grandfather, the siblings are excluded and the grandfather gets one-sixth.
This principle overrides the choice if needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الرد

ثم على قولهما : للجد حالتان إحداهما : إذا لم يكن هناك صاحب فرض : فهو مخير بين المقاسمة وبين ثلث جميع المال. والثانية : إذا كان هناك صاحب فرض: فهو مخير بين ثلاثة أشياء: إما المقاسمة، أو ثلث ما بقي، أو سدس جميع المال. بيانه : جد وأخ: للجد: النصف، وللأخ: النصف. جد وأخوان: الثلث والمقاسمة هنا سواء. جد وثلاثة إخوة : الثلث هنا خير له من المقاسمة. فإن كان معهم صاحب فرض: أعطي فرضه، ثم يُنظر إلى ثلث ما بقي، وإلى سدس جميع المال وإلى المقاسمة: يُنظر أولاً إلى ثلث ما بقي، وإلى سدس جميع المال : أيهما خير له، ثم يُنظر إلى خيرهما، وإلى المقاسمة : فأيهما كان خيراً له : كان له. بيانه: بنت وجد وأخٌ للبنت النصفُ، والباقي بينهما نصفان؛ لأن المقاسمة خير له من ثلث ما بقي، ومن سدس المال. فإن كانا أخوين والمسألة بحالها فهنا ثلث ما بقي، وسدس جميع المال، والمقاسمة سواء. فإن كانوا ثلاثةً وهي بحالها فثلث الباقي، وهو سدس جميع المال خير له من المقاسمة. بنتان وجد وأخوان لأب وأم للابنتين: الثلثان، وما بقي وهو يُعطى الجد منه سدس جميع المال ؛ لأن ذلك خير له من المقاسمة، ومن ثلث الباقي. وإن ترك ابنتين وجداً وأختاً لأب وأم: فللابنتين: الثلثان، وما بقي فهو للجد والأخت، للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين؛ لأن المقاسمة خير له من السدس ومن ثلث ما بقي. ولو زاد في الفريضة فريضةً أخرى، كابنتين وأم وجد وأخ لأب وأم، أو أخت فللابنتين الثلثان وللأم السدس، وبقي السدس يُعطى للجد؛ لأن مذهب زيد : أن نصيب الجد لا ينتقص من السدس، ولا شيء للأخ أو الأخت ؛ لأن الأخت ها هنا عصبة.
Chapter of Return. Then according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the grandfather has two states. One: if there is no fixed-share heir, he has the choice between division (muqasama) and one-third of the entire estate. The second: if there is a fixed-share heir, he has the choice between three things: either division, or one-third of what remains, or one-sixth of the entire estate. Its explanation: grandfather and brother: for the grandfather half, for the brother half. Grandfather and two brothers: one-third and division here are equal. Grandfather and three brothers: one-third here is better for him than division. If there is with them a fixed-share heir: he is given his fixed share, then one looks at one-third of what remains and one-sixth of the entire estate and division: first one looks at one-third of what remains and one-sixth of the entire estate: whichever is better for him, then one looks at the better of the two and division: whichever is better for him is his. Its explanation: daughter, grandfather, and brother: for the daughter half, and the remainder between them halves; because division is better for him than one-third of what remains and than one-sixth of the estate. If there are two brothers and the case is as before, then here one-third of what remains, one-sixth of the entire estate, and division are equal. If there are three and it is as before, then one-third of the remainder, which is one-sixth of the entire estate, is better for him than division. Two daughters, grandfather, and two full brothers: for the two daughters two-thirds, and what remains, which is one-third, is given to the grandfather from it as one-sixth of the entire estate; because that is better for him than division or one-third of the remainder. And if he leaves two daughters, a grandfather, and a full sister: for the two daughters two-thirds, and what remains is for the grandfather and the sister, for the male the portion of two females; because division is better for him than one-sixth or one-third of what remains. And if one adds another heir to the estate, like two daughters, mother, grandfather, and full brother or sister: for the two daughters two-thirds, for the mother one-sixth, and one-sixth remains, given to the grandfather; because the madhhab of Zayd is that the portion of the grandfather does not fall below one-sixth, and nothing for the brother or sister; because the sister here is 'asaba (residuary).
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary explaining the two states of the grandfather when inheriting alongside siblings (full or half? the text says 'akh' generally but examples use 'akh li ab wa umm') according to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn). The grandfather is a special heir in the Hanafi school; his share is not fixed like the Quranic sharers but he is given choices to maximize his inheritance. If no fixed-share heir exists, he chooses between equal division with siblings (مُقَاسَمَة) or taking one-third of the total estate — whichever is better for him. If a fixed-share heir is present, he compares three options: مقاسمة, one-third of the residue, or one-sixth of the entire estate. Through worked examples, the text demonstrates that the grandfather always receives the highest possible share. In the last example, with the mother and two daughters, the grandfather gets a full one-sixth because the view of Zayd ibn Thabit is followed: the grandfather's share never falls below one-sixth, and the siblings are excluded altogether by the daughter and mother combination. This passage implicitly confirms the Hanafi reliance on Zayd's opinion in certain faraid matters.

Key Terms
الجد (al-jadd): The paternal grandfather (father's father) in inheritance; treated as a special heir who receives the best of multiple share options when inheriting with siblings.
المقاسمة (al-muqasamah): Division of the estate between the grandfather and siblings as if the grandfather were a brother; he takes a share equal to one brother's share.
صاحب فرض (sahib fard): A Qur'anic sharer entitled to a fixed fraction (e.g., daughter takes 1/2, wife 1/4, mother 1/6).
ثلث ما بقي (thuluth ma baqi): One-third of the residue after fixed shares are given to the صاحب فرض heirs.
سدس جميع المال (sudus jami' al-mal): One-sixth of the total estate before any distribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, when a fixed-share heir is present, which options does the grandfather compare?
A) Muqasamah, one-third of the residue, or one-sixth of the total estate
B) One-half, one-third, or one-sixth
C) Muqasamah or one-third of the total estate only
D) One-sixth of the total estate or one-third of the residue

Key Takeaway
The grandfather's share is the maximum of muqasamah, one-third of residue, and one-sixth of total, with a floor of one-sixth from Zayd's madhhab.

The Share of Grandmothers When Multiple Are Present
States that the sixth goes to the nearest grandmother and cites differences between Ali and Zaid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for distributing the sixth among multiple grandmothers and explain the difference between the views of Imam Ali (and Abu Hanifa) and Zayd ibn Thabit.

Core Idea
Only the nearest grandmother inherits the sixth—regardless of whether she is from the father's or mother's side.

In inheritance law, grandmothers are entitled to one-sixth of the estate when certain conditions are met. But when multiple grandmothers exist, which one receives the share? This lesson explains the Hanafi position, which prioritizes the closest grandmother by lineage, and contrasts it with the view of Zayd ibn Thabit.

Guided Path
1
State the default rule
The text opens with the statement: 'the sixth belongs to the nearest of them.' This is the baseline ruling—only the closest grandmother inherits.
2
Identify the two opinions
Imam Ali (and Abu Hanifa) hold that the nearest grandmother from either side takes the whole sixth. Zayd ibn Thabit differentiates: if the nearer is from the mother's side, she takes it alone; if from the father's side, the farther from the mother's side shares equally.
The dispute is over what happens when the near grandmother is paternal.
3
Analyze Zayd's position
Zayd's view gives a share to a more distant maternal grandmother when the nearer is paternal. This means the maternal side is never completely excluded.
This is the key difference from the Hanafi view.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school follows Imam Ali: the nearest grandmother, regardless of side, takes the entire sixth. No sharing occurs.
This simplifies distribution and avoids splitting the sixth.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi, if the nearer grandmother is paternal, she takes all six; under Zayd, she shares with the farther maternal grandmother. The actual division changes depending on which view is adopted.
This difference affects who receives how much in real cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا اجتمعت الجدات : فالسدس لأقربهنَّ. اعلم أنه إذا كان بعض الجدات أقرب من بعض، فإن علياً كرم الله وجهه يجعل السدس للقُربى من أي جهة كانت. وبه قال أبو حنيفة. وعن زيد : إن كانت القربى من جهة الأم: فالسدس لها. وإن كانت من جهة الأب : شاركتها البعدى من جهة الأم.
And if grandmothers gather (together), then the sixth belongs to the nearest of them. Know that if some grandmothers are closer than others, Ali (may Allah honor his face) makes the sixth for the nearer from whichever side she is. And Abu Hanifa said the same. And from Zayd: if the nearer is from the mother's side, the sixth is for her. And if she is from the father's side, the farther (grandmother) from the mother's side shares with her.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding the inheritance of the sixth share (السدس) when multiple grandmothers exist. The default rule is that only the closest in lineage to the deceased inherits the sixth; more distant grandmothers are excluded. Here, two opinions are cited: Imam Ali (رضي الله عنه) and Abu Hanifa hold that regardless of whether the closer grandmother is from the mother's or father's side, she alone takes the whole sixth. Zayd ibn Thabit (رضي الله عنه) differs: if the closer grandmother is from the mother's side, she takes the entire sixth; but if the closer is from the father's side, then the (more distant) grandmother from the mother's side shares the sixth equally with her. The Hanafi school follows the view of Ali and Abu Hanifa, giving the entire sixth exclusively to the nearest grandmother irrespective of side.

Key Terms
الجدات (al-jaddat): Grandmothers collectively, both maternal and paternal; text deals with prioritizing among them for the sixth share.
أقربهن (aqrabuhunna): The nearest in lineage to the deceased among grandmothers, determined by degree of relation (e.g., mother's mother is closer than mother's mother's mother).
جهة الأم/الأب (jihat al-umm/al-ab): Side of lineage: maternal (through mother) or paternal (through father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) All grandmothers share the sixth equally

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance, only the nearest grandmother inherits the sixth, regardless of whether she is from the father's or mother's side.

The Closest Grandmother Takes the Sixth: Hanafi Rule and Companion Differences
Commentary on the rule that the closest grandmother takes the sixth, with companion ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for multiple grandmothers and apply it to simple cases, distinguishing the positions of Ali, Abu Hanifa, Zayd, and Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
The closest grandmother excludes all others from the sixth, regardless of side.

When multiple grandmothers survive, the key question is which one inherits the fixed sixth. This lesson explores the dominant Hanafi position and the differences among early authorities.

Guided Path
1
List all grandmothers
Identify each grandmother by her relationship to the deceased (e.g., mother's mother, father's mother's mother). Determine how many generations separate her from the deceased.
The distance is measured by the number of intermediate ancestors.
2
Identify the closest grandmother(s)
Compare the generational distances. The one with the fewest intermediate ancestors is the closest.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
Award the entire sixth to the closest grandmother. If multiple are equally close, they share the sixth equally.
This is the position of Imam Ali and Abu Hanifa.
4
Note the companion variations
Zayd ibn Thabit distinguishes based on side: if the closest is from the father's side, the distant from the mother's side shares. Ibn Mas'ud gives the sixth to all grandmothers, near and distant, but if both are from father's side, he prefers the nearer.
These views are not relied upon in the Hanafi school.

Chapter of Radd. And when grandmothers are together, then the sixth is for the closest among them. * His saying: 'And when grandmothers are together, then the sixth is for the closest among them.' Know that when some grandmothers are closer than others, 'Ali (may Allah honor his face) assigns the sixth to the nearer one from whichever side, and his companions. And Abu Hanifa said likewise. And from Zayd: If the nearer is from the mother's side, the sixth is for her. And if from the father's side, the distant one from the mother's side shares with her. And Ibn Mas'ud would give inheritance to both the near and the distant from whichever side. - If from the father's side there is a near and a distant, he gave inheritance to the nearer. Example: Mother's mother and father's mother's mother. Abu Hanifa said: the sixth is for the mother's mother. In Ibn Mas'ud's view, it is between them. Mother's father and father's mother's mother: according to Abu Hanifa, the sixth is for the father's mother because she is nearer; and from Zayd, it is between them. Father's father's mother and mother's mother's mother's mother: according to Abu Hanifa, the sixth is for the father's mother. And on Zayd's statement, it is between them. And when a grandmother has two relationships, according to Muhammad and Zufar she has the share of two grandmothers, and according to Abu Yusuf she has the share of one grandmother. Explanation: A man married his maternal aunt's daughter, and she gave birth to a son. The man's grandmother is his mother's mother – she is also the grandmother of this son as his mother's mother's mother, and also his grandmother as his father's mother's mother. If the man dies leaving his grandmother (his father's mother), then this son dies leaving these two grandmothers. According to Muhammad and Zufar, the one with two relationships gets two-thirds of the sixth, and the other who is the father's father's mother gets one-third of the sixth.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the faraid rule: 'When grandmothers are together, the sixth is for the closest among them.' The commentator explains the different positions of the Companions and the Hanafi school. According to Imam Ali and Abu Hanifa, the sixth goes exclusively to the closest grandmother, regardless of whether she is from the mother's or father's side. Imam Zayd distinguishes: if the closest is from the mother's side, she alone takes the sixth; but if the closest is from the father's side, the distant grandmother from the mother's side shares the sixth equally. Ibn Mas'ud gives the sixth to both the near and distant grandmothers from any side, but if there is both a near and a distant from the father's side, he favors the nearer. The commentary provides concrete examples: e.g., if the grandmothers are the mother's mother (near) and the father's mother's mother (distant), Abu Hanifa gives the sixth to the mother's mother; Ibn Mas'ud gives it to both equally. The passage then addresses a special case: a grandmother who has two relationships to the deceased (e.g., she is both the mother's mother and the father's mother's mother). Here, the Hanafi imams differ: Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar hold that she inherits as two grandmothers, thus taking two-thirds of the sixth (i.e., two shares out of three if there are three grandmothers), while Imam Abu Yusuf holds that she inherits as one grandmother, taking only one share. The practical illustration involves a man who marries his maternal aunt, producing a son; the grandmother becomes related to the son on both sides through different chains. When the son dies leaving that grandmother and another grandmother, Muhammad and Zufar allocate two-thirds of the sixth to the dual-relationship grandmother and one-third to the other, whereas Abu Yusuf gives each one share if there are three shares total (but the text says one share for each). The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Yusuf, but the commentary presents both views.

Key Terms
جدة (jaddah): Grandmother; an heir entitled to the sixth in the absence of mother.
سدس (suds): One-sixth of the estate; the fixed share for a single grandmother.
قربى (qurba): The closer grandmother in terms of generational distance to the deceased.
قرابتان (qarabatan): A grandmother who is related to the deceased through both her mother and father, i.e., two distinct lineages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Zayd ibn Thabit
B) Abdullah ibn Mas'ud
C) Imam Ali
D) Umar ibn al-Khattab

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, following Imam Ali, awards the sixth to the closest grandmother, excluding all others.

The Dual-Relationship Grandmother: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Share Calculation
Commentary on the rule for a grandmother with dual relationships, with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compute the inheritance shares for a grandmother with dual relationships according to the views of Muhammad/Zufar and Abu Yusuf, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A grandmother with dual relationships inherits as one person; Abu Yusuf gives her one share, Muhammad and Zufar give two.

When a grandmother is connected to the deceased through both her mother and father, a unique question arises: does she inherit as one person or as two? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Muhammad/Zufar and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dual relationship
Determine if any grandmother is simultaneously related through the mother's line and the father's line (e.g., she is both the mother's mother's mother and the father's mother).
The example in the text: a man's mother's mother becomes the grandmother of his son through multiple paths.
2
Note the total share
The grandmothers' collective share is one sixth of the estate.
3
Apply Muhammad/Zufar's view
Count the dual-relationship grandmother as two separate grandmothers. If there are two grandmothers total (one dual, one single), the dual gets two shares out of three, i.e., two-thirds of the sixth. The other gets one-third.
This gives her 2/3 of the sixth.
4
Apply Abu Yusuf's view
Count the dual-relationship grandmother as one person. She and any other grandmother share the sixth equally. If there are two grandmothers, each gets one-half of the sixth.
This gives her 1/2 of the sixth.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Yusuf's view, because a single person cannot inherit multiple shares from the same estate.
Later Hanafi scholars affirm this tarjih.

Source Text

وإذا كان للجدة قرابتان فعند محمد :وزفر لها نصيب جدتين.
وعند أبي يوسف: لها نصيب جدة واحدة.
:
بيانه: رجل تزوج بنت خالته ، فولدت له ولداً: فإن جدة الرجل أُمُّ أمه جدة هذا الولد أم أم أمه، وهي أيضاً جدته أم أم أبيه.
فإن مات الرجل، وخلّف جدته أم أبيه، ثم مات هذا الولد، وخلف
هاتين الجدتين :
فعلى قول محمد وزفر : لصاحبة القرابتين ثلثا السدس، وللأخرى التي هي أم أبي الأب: : ثلث السدس.
Chapter of Radd. And when grandmothers are together, then the sixth is for the closest among them. * His saying: 'And when grandmothers are together, then the sixth is for the closest among them.' Know that when some grandmothers are closer than others, 'Ali (may Allah honor his face) assigns the sixth to the nearer one from whichever side, and his companions. And Abu Hanifa said likewise. And from Zayd: If the nearer is from the mother's side, the sixth is for her. And if from the father's side, the distant one from the mother's side shares with her. And Ibn Mas'ud would give inheritance to both the near and the distant from whichever side. - If from the father's side there is a near and a distant, he gave inheritance to the nearer. Example: Mother's mother and father's mother's mother. Abu Hanifa said: the sixth is for the mother's mother. In Ibn Mas'ud's view, it is between them. Mother's father and father's mother's mother: according to Abu Hanifa, the sixth is for the father's mother because she is nearer; and from Zayd, it is between them. Father's father's mother and mother's mother's mother's mother: according to Abu Hanifa, the sixth is for the father's mother. And on Zayd's statement, it is between them. And when a grandmother has two relationships, according to Muhammad and Zufar she has the share of two grandmothers, and according to Abu Yusuf she has the share of one grandmother. Explanation: A man married his maternal aunt's daughter, and she gave birth to a son. The man's grandmother is his mother's mother – she is also the grandmother of this son as his mother's mother's mother, and also his grandmother as his father's mother's mother. If the man dies leaving his grandmother (his father's mother), then this son dies leaving these two grandmothers. According to Muhammad and Zufar, the one with two relationships gets two-thirds of the sixth, and the other who is the father's father's mother gets one-third of the sixth.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the faraid rule: 'When grandmothers are together, the sixth is for the closest among them.' The commentator explains the different positions of the Companions and the Hanafi school. According to Imam Ali and Abu Hanifa, the sixth goes exclusively to the closest grandmother, regardless of whether she is from the mother's or father's side. Imam Zayd distinguishes: if the closest is from the mother's side, she alone takes the sixth; but if the closest is from the father's side, the distant grandmother from the mother's side shares the sixth equally. Ibn Mas'ud gives the sixth to both the near and distant grandmothers from any side, but if there is both a near and a distant from the father's side, he favors the nearer. The commentary provides concrete examples: e.g., if the grandmothers are the mother's mother (near) and the father's mother's mother (distant), Abu Hanifa gives the sixth to the mother's mother; Ibn Mas'ud gives it to both equally. The passage then addresses a special case: a grandmother who has two relationships to the deceased (e.g., she is both the mother's mother and the father's mother's mother). Here, the Hanafi imams differ: Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar hold that she inherits as two grandmothers, thus taking two-thirds of the sixth (i.e., two shares out of three if there are three grandmothers), while Imam Abu Yusuf holds that she inherits as one grandmother, taking only one share. The practical illustration involves a man who marries his maternal aunt, producing a son; the grandmother becomes related to the son on both sides through different chains. When the son dies leaving that grandmother and another grandmother, Muhammad and Zufar allocate two-thirds of the sixth to the dual-relationship grandmother and one-third to the other, whereas Abu Yusuf gives each one share if there are three shares total (but the text says one share for each). The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Yusuf, but the commentary presents both views.

Key Terms
جدة (jaddah): Grandmother; an heir entitled to the sixth in the absence of mother.
سدس (suds): One-sixth of the estate; the fixed share for a single grandmother.
قربى (qurba): The closer grandmother in terms of generational distance to the deceased.
قرابتان (qarabatan): A grandmother who is related to the deceased through both her mother and father, i.e., two distinct lineages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two-thirds of the sixth
B) One-half of the sixth
C) The entire sixth
D) Nothing, she is excluded

Key Takeaway
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, a grandmother with two relationships to the deceased inherits as one person, receiving one share of the grandmothers' sixth.

Dispute over grandmother inheritance: Ibn Mas'ud, Abu Hanifa, Zaid
Presents opinions on grandmother inheritance from different sides

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the inheritance of grandmothers when there is a nearer and a more distant grandmother, and explain the opposing view of Ibn Mas'ud and Zaid bin Thabit.

Core Idea
The nearest valid grandmother inherits the entire one-sixth; more distant ones are excluded.

This passage presents a classical dispute in inheritance law (faraid) concerning multiple grandmothers from different sides. Abu Hanifa's position is that the nearest grandmother takes the full share, while Ibn Mas'ud and Zaid bin Thabit held that all grandmothers share equally. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritizes closeness in lineage over distribution among all grandmothers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contesting positions
Note that the dispute is between Abu Hanifa on one side, and Ibn Mas'ud and Zaid on the other. Abu Hanifa gives the entire 1/6 to the nearest grandmother; the others split it equally.
2
Understand the examples
The passage gives three examples: (1) mother's mother vs. father's mother's mother; (2) father's mother vs. father's mother's mother; (3) father's father's mother vs. mother's mother's mother's mother. In each, the nearer (fewer generations) is identified.
The term 'qurbā' means nearer in lineage.
3
Trace the ruling in each example
Apply Abu Hanifa's rule: the nearer takes all. E.g., in the first example, the mother's mother (2 steps) is nearer than father's mother's mother (3 steps), so she gets the 1/6. In Ibn Mas'ud's view, both share equally (each 1/12).
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is clear: under Abu Hanifa, the nearer gets the entire 1/6; under the other view, the 1/6 is split. This affects the amount each heir receives.
5
Reflect on the Hanafi principle
Abu Hanifa's position is based on the general principle that a closer relative excludes a more distant one. This principle is applied consistently in Hanafi faraid.
The principle is not explicit in the passage but is inferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وكان ابن مسعود يُورث القربى والبُعدى جميعاً من أي جهة كانت.
فإن كان من جهة الأب قربى ويُعدى: وَرَّث أقربها.

مثال ذلك: أم أم وأم أم أب قال أبو حنيفة : السدس لأم الأم.
وفي قول ابن مسعود: هو بينهما.

Chapter on Return (al-Radd). Ibn Mas'ud used to give inheritance to both near and distant [grandmothers] from whichever side they are. If [the grandmother] is from the father's side, both near and distant, he gives to the nearest. For example: mother's mother and father's mother's mother. Abu Hanifa said: one-sixth to the mother's mother. In the opinion of Ibn Mas'ud: it is between them. Father's mother and father's mother's mother: according to Abu Hanifa: one-sixth to the father's mother because she is closer, and from Zaid: it is between them. Father's father's mother and mother's mother's mother's mother: according to Abu Hanifa: one-sixth to the father's mother. And according to Zaid: it is between them.

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute regarding the inheritance of grandmothers at different degrees. Ibn Mas'ud (a companion) held that all grandmothers, whether near or distant, inherit if they come from any side, but for those from the father's side, he gives to the nearest. Abu Hanifa's position is to give the entire share (one-sixth) to the grandmother nearest in lineage, while Zaid bin Thabit held that the share should be divided equally between the two grandmothers. The examples clarify the application: when there is a mother's mother and a father's mother's mother, Abu Hanifa gives the full sixth to the mother's mother (since she is closer), while Ibn Mas'ud divides it. The text follows the Hanafi commentary tradition by first stating the matn (likely from al-Quduri) and then explaining the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
جدة (jaddah): A grandmother, specifically a female ancestor in the maternal or paternal line.
سدس (suds): One-sixth, the Quranic share prescribed for certain heirs like a grandmother.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance, when multiple grandmothers exist from different lines, the one nearest to the deceased in lineage inherits the entire one-sixth share, excluding those who are more distant.

The Double Grandmother in Hanafi Inheritance
Dispute over share of grandmother with two relationships to deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance share of a grandmother with dual relationships under the views of Muhammad/Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and Malik, and explain the practical differences.

Core Idea
A grandmother related through two lines may be counted as one or two heirs, altering the distribution.

This lesson examines a nuanced inheritance case where a single woman qualifies as both a maternal and paternal grandmother of the deceased. The Hanafi school is split on whether she receives one share or two, and the Maliki school offers a third view. We will walk through the scenario and the resulting fractions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their relationships
In the given scenario, the deceased is survived by two grandmothers: one who is both maternal and paternal grandmother (double), and another who is only paternal (father's father's mother).
The double grandmother is the mother of the deceased's mother and also the mother of the deceased's father's mother.
2
Determine the base share for grandmothers
In Hanafi faraid, grandmothers collectively inherit 1/6 of the estate if there is no mother. Here, the total share awarded to grandmothers is 1/6.
The dispute is how to allocate this 1/6 between the two grandmothers.
3
Apply the three different rulings
Muhammad and Zufar treat the double grandmother as two separate persons, giving her 2/3 of the 1/6 (1/9 of estate), and the other gets 1/3 of 1/6 (1/18). Abu Yusuf treats her as one person, giving each half of 1/6 (1/12 each). Malik gives the entire 1/6 to the double grandmother.
These outcomes derive from different interpretations of legal personality.
4
Compute the actual fractions for each view
Convert the shares to fractions of the whole estate: M/Z: double 1/9, other 1/18; AY: each 1/12; Malik: double 1/6, other 0.
Verify sums: M/Z total = 1/9+1/18=3/18=1/6; AY total = 1/12+1/12=1/6; Malik total = 1/6.
5
Compare the outcomes and understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is significant: under M/Z the double grandmother gets the largest share, under AY both are equal, under Malik the other grandmother gets nothing.
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice is often Abu Yusuf's view, but Muhammad's is also transmitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان للجدة قرابتان فعند محمد :وزفر لها نصيب جدتين.
وعند أبي يوسف: لها نصيب جدة واحدة.
:
بيانه: رجل تزوج بنت خالته ، فولدت له ولداً: فإن جدة الرجل أُمُّ أمه جدة هذا الولد أم أم أمه، وهي أيضاً جدته أم أم أبيه.
فإن مات الرجل، وخلّف جدته أم أبيه، ثم مات هذا الولد، وخلف هاتين الجدتين :
فعلى قول محمد وزفر : لصاحبة القرابتين ثلثا السدس، وللأخرى التي هي أم أبي الأب: : ثلث السدس.
وعند أبي يوسف: هو بينهما نصفان.
وعند مالك : السدس كله لصاحبة القرابتين.
When a grandmother has two relationships: according to Muhammad and Zufar, she has the share of two grandmothers. According to Abu Yusuf: she has the share of one grandmother. Explanation: A man married his maternal aunt's daughter, and she bore him a son: the man's grandmother (his mother's mother) is this son's grandmother (his mother's mother), and she is also his grandmother (his father's mother). If the man dies, leaving his grandmother (his father's mother), then this son dies, leaving these two grandmothers: According to Muhammad and Zufar, the one with two relationships gets two-thirds of the one-sixth, and the other (the father's father's mother) gets one-third of the one-sixth. According to Abu Yusuf, it is between them half and half. According to Malik, the entire one-sixth goes to the one with two relationships.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage presents a nuanced inheritance case: a woman is both the maternal grandmother (from the son's mother's side) and the paternal grandmother (from the son's father's side) of the deceased. The dispute is whether she is counted as one grandmother with one share or as two distinct grandmothers. Muhammad and Zufar (Zufar is a Hanafi imam) treat her as two grandmothers, giving her 2/3 of the 1/6 share (i.e., 1/9 of the estate) and the other grandmother (the father's father's mother) gets 1/3 of 1/6 (i.e., 1/18). Abu Yusuf treats her as one grandmother, so both receive equal halves (1/12 each). Malik gives the entire 1/6 to the double grandmother. The passage illustrates how differing views on the legal personality of the heir affect distribution.

Key Terms
قرابتان (qarabataan): Two relationships or kinship ties, here meaning the grandmother is related to the deceased through both the mother's side and the father's side.
نصيب جدتين (naseeb jaddatayn): The share of two grandmothers, i.e., two portions of the one-sixth allocated for grandmothers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) She takes the share of one grandmother, and both grandmothers share the sixth equally.

D) She inherits nothing because she is a uterine relative.

Key Takeaway
When a heir qualifies through multiple relationships, the Hanafi school has two positions: one treats the heir as multiple individuals, the other as one. The mufta bihi may vary.

The Grandfather's Hajb: When Does He Block His Mother?
Explains condition for grandfather blocking his mother's inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which the paternal grandfather blocks his mother from inheritance and apply the Hanafi rule of hajb by analogy.

Core Idea
The grandfather blocks his mother only when he himself is an heir.

The law of inheritance includes intricate rules of blocking (hajb). The grandfather's ability to block his own mother depends on a key condition: whether he himself inherits. A variant text suggests he never blocks her, but the authoritative Hanafi position clarifies the nuance. This lesson unpacks that condition and the analogy that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The matn states: 'The grandfather blocks his mother.' Note the variation that says he does not. Recognize that the rule is not absolute.
The variation indicates a need for clarification.
2
Locate the condition
The commentary states: 'This is when the grandfather is not an heir. But if he is an heir, then he blocks her.' So the condition is his own heir status.
Heir here means the grandfather is not blocked by a closer agnate like the father.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is an analogy (qiyas) to the case of the mother blocking her mother (the mother's mother). Just as the mother inherits and blocks her mother, the grandfather inherits and blocks his mother.
The shared 'illa is that the intermediate heir claims the inheritance.
4
Refine with al-Khujandi
Al-Khujandi adds that the grandfather only blocks grandmothers from his side (i.e., those who trace through him). Grandmothers from other sides are not affected.
This restricts the scope of the blocking.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويَحجُبُ الجد أمه).
وفي بعض النسخ: ولا يَحجب الجد أمه.
وهذا إذا كان الجد غير وارث، أما إذا كان وارثاً: فإنه يحجبها؛
لأنها تُدلي به، وقد استحق هذا الميراث، فلا ترث معه، كأم الأم. قال الخُجَندي: ولا يَحجُبُ الجدُّ من الجدات إلا من كان مِن قِبله.
His statement: 'The grandfather blocks his mother.' And in some copies: 'The grandfather does not block his mother.' This is when the grandfather is not an heir; but if he is an heir, then he blocks her because she traces her relationship through him, and he has already claimed this inheritance, so she does not inherit with him, like the mother's mother. Al-Khujandi said: 'The grandfather only blocks from among the grandmothers those who are from his side.'
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule of hajb (blocking) concerning the grandfather (the paternal grandfather of the deceased) and his mother (the deceased's paternal great-grandmother). The matn states the general rule that the grandfather blocks his mother, but a variant says he does not. The commentary clarifies that the blocking only occurs when the grandfather himself is an heir (i.e., not excluded by a closer male like the father). If the grandfather is not an heir, he does not block her. The analogy (qiyas) is to the case of the mother's mother: the mother blocks the mother's mother, so similarly the grandfather blocks his own mother when he inherits. Al-Khujandi adds a qualification: the grandfather only blocks those grandmothers who trace their lineage through him (i.e., from his side), not those from other sides.

Key Terms
جد (jadd): The paternal grandfather of the deceased (father's father).
حجب (hajb): Blocking or excluding another heir from inheritance, either totally (hirman) or partially (nuqsan).
أم الأم (umm al-umm): The mother's mother (maternal grandmother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The grandfather blocks his mother from inheritance only if he himself inherits; otherwise, he does not.

The Invalid Grandmother: Ruling on Umm Abi al-Umm
States a ruling about an invalid grandmother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the mother of the maternal grandfather and identify why she is classified as an invalid grandmother in Hanafi faraid.

Core Idea
Not all grandmothers inherit a fixed share; those connected through a uterine relative are only uterine relatives.

In Hanafi inheritance law, grandmothers who are connected through a male or female heir inherit a fixed share. However, not every grandmother qualifies. This lesson explains the case of the mother of the maternal grandfather, who is termed an 'invalid grandmother' (jaddah fasidah) because her link to the deceased is through a uterine relative. Understanding this distinction prevents common errors in inheritance calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Heir and Ruling
The heir in question is the mother of the maternal grandfather (umm abi al-umm). The ruling is that she does not inherit a fixed share.
2
Determine the Relationship Chain
Trace her connection to the deceased: She is the mother of the maternal grandfather. The maternal grandfather is the son of this woman, and he is a uterine relative (dhu rahim) because he is related through the mother's side.
The maternal grandfather himself is not a valid grandfather for inheritance; he is also an invalid grandfather.
3
Classify the Relative
Since she connects through her son (the maternal grandfather) who is a uterine relative, she is also classified as a uterine relative. She is called an invalid grandmother (jaddah fasidah) and her son is the invalid grandfather (jadd fasid).
Valid grandmothers are those connected through a valid line, e.g., mother's mother or father's mother.
4
Know the Consequence
As a uterine relative, she does not receive a fixed share. She can only inherit as a distant kindred (dhu rahim) after the fixed sharers and residuaries are exhausted, and that too without a prescribed fraction.
This ruling applies only in Hanafi faraid; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولا ترثُ أمُّ أبي الأم بسهم)؛ لأنها رحم، فهي من جملة ذوي الأرحام، ولأنها تُدلي بابنها وهو من ذوي الأرحام، وتسمى هذه: الجدة الفاسدة، وابنها: الجد الفاسد.
His statement: 'The mother of the maternal grandfather does not inherit a share' because she is a relative, so she is among the uterine relatives, and because she traces her relationship through her son who is from the uterine relatives. This is called the invalid grandmother, and her son is the invalid grandfather.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage explains that the mother of the maternal grandfather (i.e., the great-grandmother on the mother's father's side) does not inherit a fixed Quranic share (sahm). The reason given is that she is a rahim (a uterine relative), meaning she is not connected through a valid line of male or female inheritance. She traces through her son (the maternal grandfather), who is himself a uterine relative. Such a grandmother is termed al-jaddah al-fasidah (invalid grandmother) because she does not qualify for the prescribed 1/6 share. Her son is called al-jadd al-fasid (invalid grandfather). These relatives only inherit as distant kindred (dhawi al-arham) after the fixed shares and residuaries are exhausted.

Key Terms
أم أبي الأم (umm abi al-umm): The mother of the maternal grandfather, i.e., the great-grandmother on the mother's father's side.
جدة فاسدة (jaddah fasidah): An invalid grandmother, one who does not inherit a fixed share because her lineage to the deceased is not through a valid line of male or female heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because she traces her relationship through a uterine relative (her son).
C) Because she is already excluded by the father.
D) Because she is a grandmother from the father's side.

Key Takeaway
Only grandmothers connected through a valid male or female line inherit a fixed share; those linked through uterine relatives are invalid for fixed inheritance.

Every Grandmother Blocks Her Mother: Qiyas in Inheritance
Establishes blocking hierarchy among grandmothers via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that every grandmother blocks her mother and explain the analogical reasoning (qiyas) that derives this rule.

Core Idea
The nearer ancestor always blocks the farther; this principle extends up the female line by analogy.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the blocking (hajb) of a more distant ancestor by a nearer one is a core principle. This lesson examines how the rule that a mother blocks her own mother is extended upward by analogy: every grandmother, in turn, blocks her mother (the great-grandmother). The reasoning is based on the similarity of position (mahall) along the chain of ancestry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the established rule
Start with the base rule: a mother blocks her own mother (the maternal grandmother) from inheriting. This is the original case (asl) in the qiyas.
The rule is well-established in Hanafi faraid.
2
Recognise the new case
The text considers the grandmother's mother (i.e., any grandmother's own mother, a great-grandmother) as the new case (far'). The question is whether the grandmother blocks her mother just as the mother blocks hers.
Note that 'grandmother' here includes both maternal and paternal grandmothers.
3
Extract the effective cause (illa)
The common factor is closeness: the nearer ancestor excludes the more distant one. This illa is explicit in the phrase 'محل أم الجدة مع الجدة: كمحل الجدة مع الأم'.
This illa is jaliyy (evident) and derived by tanqih al-manat.
4
Apply the analogy
Since the illa is the same (closeness), the ruling from the asl transfers to the far'. Therefore, every grandmother blocks her own mother from inheriting the fixed share.
This ensures only the nearest eligible grandmother in each line inherits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكلُّ جدة: تحجب أمها ؛ لأن محل أم الجدة مع الجدة: كمحل الجدة مع الأم، والأم تحجُبُ أمَّها ، فكذا الجدة تحجب أمها، والله أعلم.
His statement: 'Every grandmother blocks her mother' because the position of the grandmother's mother with respect to the grandmother is like the position of the grandmother with respect to the mother, and the mother blocks her mother, so likewise the grandmother blocks her mother. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage provides a qiyas (analogical reasoning) to extend the rule of blocking from mothers to grandmothers. The rule is that the mother blocks the maternal grandmother (her own mother) from inheritance because she is closer. Similarly, any grandmother (e.g., the paternal grandmother) blocks her own mother (the great-grandmother) from the 1/6 share. The 'illa (effective cause) is closeness: the nearer ancestor excludes the more distant one. Thus, the hierarchy is maintained: the daughter (mother) blocks the mother (grandmother), and the grandmother in turn blocks her own mother (great-grandmother). This ensures that only the nearest valid grandmother in each line inherits.

Key Terms
محل (mahall): Position or status in the inheritance hierarchy, specifically in terms of proximity.
تحجب (tahjubu): Blocks or excludes from inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Hijab Rules for Grandfather and Grandmothers
Expansion on hajb rules for grandfather and grandmother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hijab rules for a grandfather over his mother and for a grandmother over her mother, and distinguish the Hanafi position from those of Abu Yusuf and Malik.

Core Idea
Closeness blocks distance: a grandfather who inherits prevents his mother, and every grandmother prevents her own mother.

This passage from the chapter on Return (al-Radd) addresses two interconnected hijab scenarios: the grandfather's preclusion of his mother (the paternal grandmother), and the preclusion of a more distant grandmother by a closer one. The text also identifies a special category, the 'invalid grandmother' who does not inherit by a fixed share. We will unpack the rulings and the analogical reasoning behind them, and then examine the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as well as the inter-madhhab difference with Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main hijab rules
The text states: (1) The grandfather prevents his mother. (2) Every grandmother prevents her mother. Note that the first rule has a condition – the grandfather must be an heir.
The wording in some copies differs: 'The grandfather does not prevent his mother.' The commentary resolves the apparent contradiction.
2
Understand the condition for the grandfather's hijab
The grandfather prevents his mother only when he himself inherits. If he is not an heir (e.g., excluded by a closer male), she inherits. The reasoning: she is connected through him, and he has taken the inheritance.
Al-Khujandi adds that the grandfather only prevents grandmothers from his own side (paternal).
3
Analyze the qiyas for grandmother blocking her mother
The grandmother preventing her mother is analogized to a mother preventing her own mother. Since a mother blocks her mother (the grandmother), a grandmother likewise blocks her mother. The position (manzila) is parallel.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) because the relationship structure is identical.
4
Examine the invalid grandmother (al-jaddah al-fasidah)
The mother of the father's mother (i.e., the great-grandmother on the father's side) is called an 'invalid grandmother' because her connection to the deceased is through a male who is a uterine relative. She does not inherit by a fixed share but may inherit as a dhu rahm when no sharers exist.
Her son (the father's mother's father) is likewise called an 'invalid grandfather'.
5
Compare the three positions on grandmother preclusion
Abu Hanifa: the closer grandmother prevents the more distant one entirely. Abu Yusuf: the share is split equally. Malik: the entire sixth goes to the grandmother with two blood relations (e.g., both maternal and paternal). The Hanafi mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is how the sixth is distributed when two grandmothers are present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الرد
ويَحْجُبُ الجد أمه .
ولا تَرِثُ أُمُّ أبي الأم بسهم . وكل جدةٍ : تَحْجُبُ أمَّها .
وعند أبي يوسف: هو بينهما نصفان.
وعند مالك : السدس كله لصاحبة القرابتين.
قوله: (وَيَحجُبُ الجد أمه).
وفي بعض النسخ: ولا يَحجب الجد أمه.
وهذا إذا كان الجد غير وارث، أما إذا كان وارثاً: فإنه يحجبها؛
لأنها تُدلي به، وقد استحق هذا الميراث، فلا ترث معه، كأم الأم. قال الخُجَندي: ولا يَحجُبُ الجدُّ من الجدات إلا من كان مِن قِبله. * قوله : ( ولا ترثُ أمُّ أبي الأم بسهم)؛ لأنها رحم، فهي من جملة ذوي الأرحام، ولأنها تُدلي بابنها وهو من ذوي الأرحام، وتسمى هذه: الجدة الفاسدة، وابنها: الجد الفاسد.
*
قوله : (وكلُّ جدة: تحجب أمها ؛ لأن محل أم الجدة مع الجدة: كمحل الجدة مع الأم، والأم تحجُبُ أمَّها ، فكذا الجدة تحجب أمها، والله
أعلم.
Chapter of Return. The grandfather prevents his mother [from inheritance]. And the mother of the father's mother does not inherit by a share. And every grandmother prevents her mother [from inheritance]. According to Abu Yusuf: it is half between them. According to Malik: the whole sixth is for the one with two relationships. His saying: (The grandfather prevents his mother). In some copies: And the grandfather does not prevent his mother. This is when the grandfather is not an heir; but if he is an heir, then he does prevent her; because she is connected through him, and he has become entitled to this inheritance, so she does not inherit with him, like the mother of the mother. Al-Khujandi said: And the grandfather only prevents from among the grandmothers those who are from his side. * His saying: (And the mother of the father's mother does not inherit by a share); because she is a relative, so she is among the uterine relatives, and because she is connected through her son who is among the uterine relatives, and this one is called the invalid grandmother, and her son the invalid grandfather. * His saying: (And every grandmother prevents her mother); because the position of the mother of the grandmother with respect to the grandmother is like the position of the grandmother with respect to the mother, and the mother prevents her mother, so likewise the grandmother prevents her mother. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Return (al-رد) addresses the hijab (preclusion) rules concerning grandmothers and the grandfather's effect on his mother. The author first states the ruling: the grandfather (jadd) prevents his mother (the paternal grandmother) from inheriting. However, a textual variant is noted where it says the grandfather does not prevent her. The commentary resolves this by explaining that the grandfather prevents his mother only when he himself is an heir; if he is not an heir, he does not prevent her. The reasoning is that the grandmother's connection to the deceased is through the grandfather, and since the grandfather has already taken the inheritance, she cannot inherit alongside him. Al-Khujandi adds that the grandfather only prevents those grandmothers who come from his side (i.e., paternal). Next, the text states that the mother of the father's mother (the great-grandmother on the father's side) does not inherit by a fixed share; she is a uterine relative (dhu rahm). She is called the invalid grandmother, and her son (the father's mother's father) is the invalid grandfather. Finally, it introduces the rule: every grandmother prevents her own mother from inheriting. This is analogized to the rule that a mother prevents her mother (the grandmother) — since the mother blocks her own mother, similarly a grandmother blocks her mother. Then two disputes are reported: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the share is divided equally between the two grandmothers (the one who is closer and the one who is more distant but has two connections), and Imam Malik holds that the entire sixth goes to the grandmother who has two blood relations (i.e., both maternal and paternal connections). The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is the one stated at the beginning: every grandmother prevents her mother, so the closer grandmother takes the share exclusively.

Key Terms
الجدة (al-jaddah): A grandmother; includes both paternal and maternal grandmothers, but here specifically the one who is a heir by a fixed share (sixth) unless blocked.
حجب (hajb): Preclusion from inheritance due to a closer heir; here it can be total (hirman) or partial (nuqsan).
الجدة الفاسدة (al-jaddah al-fasidah): An 'invalid grandmother' who is connected to the deceased through a male who is also a uterine relative (dhi rahm), such as the mother of the paternal grandfather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, when does a grandfather prevent his mother (the paternal grandmother) from inheriting?
A) Always, regardless of whether he inherits.
B) Only when the grandfather is an heir himself.
C) Only when the grandmother is also a paternal grandmother.
D) Never; a grandfather cannot prevent his mother.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, closeness in lineage is the primary determinant for hijab: a grandfather who inherits prevents his mother, and every grandmother prevents her own mother, with the closer grandmother taking the share exclusively.

Inheritance of Dhawi al-Arham: Uterine Relatives as Last Heirs
Sets the rule and proof for uterine inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for dhawi al-arham inheritance, identify the ten categories listed, and explain the Quranic proof from al-Ahzab 33:6.

Core Idea
Uterine relatives inherit only when no 'asabah or fixed-share heir exists, based on Quran 33:6.

This lesson introduces a special category of heirs: dhawi al-arham, the uterine relatives. They are not primary or secondary heirs but become entitled to the entire estate when closer relatives are absent. The passage establishes the rule, lists ten examples, and grounds the ruling in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
The passage states that dhawi al-arham inherit when the deceased has no 'asabah (residuary heir) and no fixed-share heir (sahib fard). Recognize that these two categories must be absent.
2
List the ten categories
Memorise the ten types: child of daughter, child of sister, daughter of brother, daughter of paternal uncle, maternal uncle, maternal aunt, father of mother, paternal uncle from mother, paternal aunt, child of brother from mother, and those connected through them.
The list is illustrative; any relative connected through these ten is included.
3
Understand the Quranic proof
The verse al-Ahzab 33:6 (interpreted) gives priority to blood relatives over the public treasury. This is the basis for preferring dhawi al-arham when no closer heirs exist.
The verse's generality is taken to cover all blood relations, including uterine relatives.
4
Grasp the distribution method
Inheritance among dhawi al-arham follows the principle of closeness: the nearest relative to the deceased inherits first, similar to the system for 'asabah. If multiple at the same degree, they share.
The page ends with a discussion on determining the closest, which is covered in subsequent lessons.

قوله: (وهم عشرة ولد البنت وولد الأخت، وبنتُ الأخ، وبنتُ العم، والخال والخاله، وأبو الأم، والعم من الأم، والعمة، وولد الأخ

Chapter of Uterine Relatives. And if the deceased has no residuary heir (asabah) nor a fixed-share heir (sahib fard), then his uterine relatives inherit; they are ten: the child of the daughter, the child of the sister, the daughter of the brother, the daughter of the paternal uncle, the maternal uncle and maternal aunt, the father of the mother, the paternal uncle from the mother, the paternal aunt, and the child of the brother from the mother, and those who are connected through them. Chapter of Uterine Relatives. * He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if the deceased has no residuary heir nor a fixed-share heir: his uterine relatives inherit). The basis for this is that uterine relatives are more entitled to inheritance than the public treasury (bayt al-mal) because of His saying, the Exalted: 'And those of kinship relations are more entitled to one another in the decree of Allah' (Al-Ahzab: 6). His saying: (And they are ten: the child of the daughter, the child of the sister, the daughter of the brother, the daughter of the paternal uncle, the maternal uncle and maternal aunt, the father of the mother, the paternal uncle from the mother, the paternal aunt, and the child of the brother from the mother, and those who are connected through them). Then the inheritance of uterine relatives is like the inheritance of residuary heirs: the closest inherits over the next closest to the deceased, except that the discussion concerns knowing the closest.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on uterine relatives (dhawi al-arham). The ruling is clear: when a deceased person has neither a residuary heir (asabah) nor a fixed-share heir (like a spouse, parent, or daughter), then the estate goes to his uterine relatives. The author lists ten categories of such relatives, but notes 'and those connected through them,' indicating that the list is not exhaustive; any relative who connects through these ten is also included. The proof is from the Quran (33:6), which gives priority to those bound by blood ties over the public treasury. The method of distribution among dhawi al-arham is based on closeness to the deceased, similar to asabah (residuary heirs): the nearest in degree inherits, and if there are multiple at the same degree, they share. The text mentions that the discussion lies in determining who is closest, but the page cuts off; the remaining lesson would explain the detailed rules of proximity. In practice, the closeness is determined by the number of steps from the deceased, and sometimes by the strength of connection (e.g., two relations versus one).

Key Terms
ذوو الأرحام (dhawi al-arham): Uterine relatives who are neither residuary heirs (asabah) nor fixed-share heirs; they inherit when no such heirs exist.
العصبة (al-'asabah): Residuary heirs who take the remainder after fixed shares, or all if no fixed shares; they are typically male agnates.

Key Terms from Source Passage
